                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             Harry PotterFrom Wikipedia, the free encyclopediaThis article is about the fantasy book series. For the titular character, see  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" \o "Harry Potter (character)" Harry Potter (character). For the film series, see  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" \o "Harry Potter (film series)" Harry Potter (film series). For related topics, see HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Harry_Potter_related_topics" \o "List of Harry Potter related topics" List of Harry Potter related topics. RowlingCountry HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom" \o "United Kingdom" United KingdomLanguageEnglishGenre HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasy_literature" \o "Fantasy literature" Fantasy,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young-adult_fiction" \o "Young-adult fiction" young-adult fiction, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mystery_(fiction)" \o "Mystery (fiction)" mystery,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thriller_(genre)" \o "Thriller (genre)" thriller,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bildungsroman" \o "Bildungsroman" Bildungsroman, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magical_realism" \o "Magical realism" magical realismPublisher HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomsbury_Publishing" \o "Bloomsbury Publishing" Bloomsbury Publishing (UK) HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_A._Levine_Books" \o "Arthur A. Levine Books" Arthur A. Levine Books (US)Published29 June 1997 – 21 July 2007 (initial publication)Media typePrint (hardback & paperback) HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Audiobook" \o "Audiobook" Audiobook HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E-book" \o "E-book" E-book (as of March 2012) HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-1" [1]No. of books7Harry Potter is a series of seven  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasy_literature" \o "Fantasy literature" fantasy novels written by the British author  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Rowling" \o "J. K. Rowling" J. K. Rowling. The series, named after the titular character, chronicles the adventures of a young  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magician_(fantasy)" \o "Magician (fantasy)" wizard,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" \o "Harry Potter (character)" Harry Potter, and his friends  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Weasley" \o "Ron Weasley" Ronald Weasley and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermione_Granger" \o "Hermione Granger" Hermione Granger, all of whom are students at  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hogwarts_School_of_Witchcraft_and_Wizardry" \o "Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry" Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry. The main  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Story_arc" \o "Story arc" story arc concerns Harry's quest to overcome the Dark wizard  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" \o "Lord Voldemort" Lord Voldemort, who aims to become immortal, conquer the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_universe" \o "Harry Potter universe" wizarding world, subjugate non-magical people, and destroy all those who stand in his way, especially Harry Potter.Since the release of the first novel,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" \o "Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone" Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone, on 30 June 1997, the books have gained immense popularity, critical acclaim, and commercial success worldwide. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-2" [2] The series has also had some share of criticism, including concern for the increasingly dark tone. As of July 2013, the book series had sold between 400 and 450 million copies, making it one of the HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_best-selling_books" \o "List of best-selling books" best-selling book series in history, and had been  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_in_translation" \o "Harry Potter in translation" translated into 73 languages. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Translations_for_Harry_Potter-3" [3] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-PotterStats20130731-4" [4] The last four books consecutively set records as the fastest-selling books in history, with the final instalment selling approximately 11 million copies in the United States within the first twenty-four hours of its release.A series of many  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genre" \o "Genre" genres, including  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasy" \o "Fantasy" fantasy,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coming_of_age" \o "Coming of age" coming of age, and the British  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_story" \o "School story" school story, (with elements of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mystery_(fiction)" \o "Mystery (fiction)" mystery,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thriller_(genre)" \o "Thriller (genre)" thriller,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adventure_novel" \o "Adventure novel" adventure, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romance_novel" \o "Romance novel" romance), it has many cultural meanings and references. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-meanings-5" [5] According to Rowling, the main  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theme_(literature)" \o "Theme (literature)" theme is death. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Geordie_Greig-6" [6] There are also many other themes in the series, such as prejudice and corruption. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-QuickQuoteQuill-7" [7]The series was originally printed in English by two major publishers,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomsbury_Publishing" \o "Bloomsbury Publishing" Bloomsbury in the United Kingdom and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholastic_Corporation" \o "Scholastic Corporation" Scholastic Press in the United States. The books have since been published by many publishers worldwide. The books, with the seventh book split into two parts, have been made into an eight-part  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_(film_series)" \o "Harry Potter (film series)" film series by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros." \o "Warner Bros." Warner Bros. Pictures, the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" \o "List of highest-grossing franchises and film series" highest-grossing film series of all time. The series also originated much  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tie-in" \o "Tie-in" tie-in merchandise, making the Harry Potter brand worth in excess of $15 billion. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-HP_brand_worth-8" [8]Thanks to the success of the books and films, Harry Potter has also been used for a theme park,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wizarding_World_of_Harry_Potter_(Islands_of_Adventure)" \o "The Wizarding World of Harry Potter (Islands of Adventure)" The Wizarding World of Harry Potter in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Parks_%26_Resorts" \o "Universal Parks & Resorts" Universal Parks & Resorts'  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islands_of_Adventure" \o "Islands of Adventure" Islands of Adventure.Contents HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Plot" 1 Plot HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l series HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Achievements" 5 Achievements HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Cultural_impact" 5.1 Cultural impact 5.3 Awards, honours, and recognition HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Reception" 6 Reception HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Literary_criticism" 6.1 Literary criticism HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Social_impacts" 6.2 Social impacts HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Controversies" 6.3 Controversies HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Adaptations" 7 Adaptations HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Films" 7.1 Films HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Games" 7.2 Games HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Audiobooks" 7.3 Audiobooks HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Stage_production" 7.4 Stage production HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Attractions" 8 Attractions HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "United_States" 8.1 United States HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "United_Kingdom" 8.2 United Kingdom HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "See_also" 9 See also HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "References" 10 References HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "Further_reading" 11 Further reading HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "External_links" 12 External linksPlotFurther information:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_universe" \o "Harry Potter universe" Harry Potter universeThe novels revolve around  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" \o "Harry Potter (character)" Harry Potter, an orphan who discovers at the age of eleven that he is a wizard, living within the ordinary world of non-magical people, known as HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muggles" \o "Muggles" Muggles. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-9" [9] His ability is inborn and such children are invited to attend an exclusive magic school that teaches the necessary skills to succeed in the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wizarding_world" \o "Wizarding world" wizarding world. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-muggle_guide-10" [10] Harry becomes a student at  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hogwarts" \o "Hogwarts" Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry and it is here where most of the events in the series take place. As Harry develops through his adolescence, he learns to overcome the problems that face him: magical, social and emotional, including ordinary teenage challenges such as friendships, infatuation and exams, and the greater test of preparing himself for the confrontation in the real world that lies ahead. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-11" [11]Each book chronicles one year in Harry's life HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-12" [12] with the main narrative being set in the years 1991–98. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-13" [13] The books also contain many  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flashback_(narrative)" \o "Flashback (narrative)" flashbacks, which are frequently experienced by Harry viewing the memories of other characters in a device called a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pensieve" \o "Pensieve" Pensieve.The environment Rowling created is completely separate from reality yet also intimately connected to it. While the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasy_world" \o "Fantasy world" fantasy land of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narnia_(world)" \o "Narnia (world)" Narnia is an  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_universe_(fiction)" \o "Parallel universe (fiction)" alternative universe and the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_of_the_Rings" \o "Lord of the Rings" Lord of the Rings'  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle-earth" \o "Middle-earth" Middle-earth a mythic past, the wizarding world of Harry Potter exists in parallel within the real world and contains magical versions of the ordinary elements of everyday life. Many of its institutions and locations are recognisable, such as London. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-14" [14] It comprises a fragmented collection of overlooked hidden streets, ancient pubs, lonely country manors and secluded castles that remain invisible to the Muggle population. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-muggle_guide-10" [10]Early yearsWhen the first novel of the series,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" \o "Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone" Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone (published in some countries as Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone), opens, it is apparent that some significant event has taken place in the wizarding world—an event so very remarkable, even the Muggles notice signs of it. The full background to this event and to the person of Harry Potter is only revealed gradually through the series. After the introductory chapter, the book leaps forward to a time shortly before Harry Potter's eleventh birthday, and it is at this point that his magical background begins to be revealed.Harry's first contact with the wizarding world is through a half-giant,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rubeus_Hagrid" \o "Rubeus Hagrid" Rubeus Hagrid, keeper of grounds and keys at Hogwarts. Hagrid reveals some of Harry's history. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-stories-15" [15] Harry learns that as a baby he witnessed his parents' murder by the power-obsessed Dark wizard  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" \o "Lord Voldemort" Lord Voldemort, who then attempted to kill him also. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-stories-15" [15] For reasons not immediately revealed, the spell with which Voldemort tried to kill Harry rebounded. Harry survived with only a lightning-shaped scar on his forehead as a memento of the attack, and Voldemort disappeared afterwards. As its inadvertent saviour from Voldemort's reign of terror, Harry has become a living legend in the wizarding world. However, at the orders of the venerable and well-known wizard  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" \o "Albus Dumbledore" Albus Dumbledore, the orphaned Harry had been placed in the home of his unpleasant  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muggle" \o "Muggle" Muggle relatives, the Dursleys, who had him safe but hid his true heritage from him in hopes that he would grow up "normal". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-stories-15" [15]With Hagrid's help, Harry prepares for and undertakes his first year of study at Hogwarts. As Harry begins to explore the magical world, the reader is introduced to many of the primary locations used throughout the series. Harry meets most of the main characters and gains his two closest friends:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Weasley" \o "Ron Weasley" Ron Weasley, a fun-loving member of an ancient, large, happy, but poor wizarding family, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermione_Granger" \o "Hermione Granger" Hermione Granger, a gifted and very hardworking witch of non-magical parentage. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-stories-15" [15] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-16" [16] Harry also encounters the school's potions master, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Severus_Snape" \o "Severus Snape" Severus Snape, who displays a deep and abiding dislike for him, and the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defence_Against_the_Dark_Arts" \o "Defence Against the Dark Arts" Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quirinus_Quirrell" \o "Quirinus Quirrell" Quirinus Quirrell, who later turns out to be controlled by Lord Voldemort. The plot concludes with Harry's second confrontation with Lord Voldemort, who in his quest for immortality, yearns to gain the power of the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorcerer%27s_Stone" \o "Sorcerer's Stone" Philosopher's Stone, a substance that bestow everlasting life. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-stories-15" [15]The series continues with  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" \o "Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets" Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets describing Harry's second year at Hogwarts. He and his friends investigate a 50-year-old mystery that appears tied to recent sinister events at the school. Ron's younger sister,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ginny_Weasley" \o "Ginny Weasley" Ginny Weasley, enrols in her first year at Hogwarts, and finds an old notebook which turns out to be Voldemort's diary from his school days. Ginny becomes possessed by Voldemort through the diary and unconsciously opens the "Chamber of Secrets," unleashing an ancient monster which begins attacking students at Hogwarts. The novel delves into the history of Hogwarts and a legend revolving around the Chamber that soon frightened everyone in the school. The book also introduces a new  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defence_Against_the_Dark_Arts" \o "Defence Against the Dark Arts" Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilderoy_Lockhart" \o "Gilderoy Lockhart" Gilderoy Lockhart, a highly cheerful, self-conceited know-it-all who later turns out to be a fraud. For the first time, Harry realises that racial prejudice exists in the wizarding world even before, and he learns that Voldemort's reign of terror was often directed at wizards who were descended from Muggles. Harry also learns that his ability to speak  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parseltongue" \o "Parseltongue" Parseltongue, the language of snakes, is rare and often associated with the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_magic" \o "Black magic" Dark Arts. The novel ends after Harry saves Ginny's life by destroying a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basilisk_(Harry_Potter)" \o "Basilisk (Harry Potter)" basilisk and the enchanted diary which has been the source of the problems.The third novel,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" \o "Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban" Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban, follows Harry in his third year of magical education. It is the only book in the series which does not feature Lord Voldemort. Instead, Harry must deal with the knowledge that he has been targeted by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirius_Black" \o "Sirius Black" Sirius Black, an escaped mass murderer believed to have assisted in the deaths of Harry's parents. As Harry struggles with his reaction to the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dementors" \o "Dementors" dementors—dark creatures with the power to devour a human soul—which are ostensibly protecting the school, he reaches out to  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remus_Lupin" \o "Remus Lupin" Remus Lupin, a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defence_Against_the_Dark_Arts" \o "Defence Against the Dark Arts" Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher who is eventually revealed to be a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Werewolf" \o "Werewolf" werewolf. Lupin teaches Harry defensive measures which are well above the level of magic generally executed by people his age. Harry learns that both Lupin and Black were best friends of his father and that Black was framed by their fourth friend,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Pettigrew" \o "Peter Pettigrew" Peter Pettigrew. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-plot-azkaban-17" [17] In this book, a recurring theme throughout the series is emphasised—in every book there is a new Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher, none of whom lasts more than one school year.Voldemort returns HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_elephant_house.jpg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/The_elephant_house.jpg/200px-The_elephant_house.jpg" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_elephant_house.jpg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET " HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Elephant_House_(Edinburgh_Caf%C3%A9)" \o "The Elephant House (Edinburgh Café)" The Elephant House" – The café in Edinburgh in which Rowling wrote the first part of Harry Potter.During Harry's fourth year of school (detailed in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" \o "Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire" Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire) Harry is unwillingly entered as a participant in the Triwizard Tournament, a dangerous contest where Harry must compete against a witch and a wizard "champion" from visiting schools as well as another Hogwarts student, causing Harry's friends to distance themselves from him.  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-plot-goblet-18" [18] Harry is guided through the tournament by their new Defence Against the Dark Arts professor,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mad-Eye_Moody" \o "Mad-Eye Moody" Alastor "Mad-Eye" Moody, who turns out to be an impostor—one of Voldemort's supporters named  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barty_Crouch,_Jr" \o "Barty Crouch, Jr" Barty Crouch, Jr. in disguise. The point at which the mystery is unravelled marks the series' shift from foreboding and uncertainty into open conflict. Voldemort's plan to have Crouch use the tournament to bring Harry to Voldemort succeeds. Although Harry manages to escape, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Diggory" \o "Cedric Diggory" Cedric Diggory, the other Hogwarts champion in the tournament, is killed by Peter Pettigrew and Voldemort re-enters the wizarding world with a physical body.In the fifth book,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" \o "Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix" Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix, Harry must confront the newly resurfaced Voldemort. In response to Voldemort's reappearance, Dumbledore re-activates the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Phoenix_(organisation)" \o "Order of the Phoenix (organisation)" Order of the Phoenix, a secret society which works from Sirius Black's dark family home to defeat Voldemort's minions and protect Voldemort's targets, especially Harry. Despite Harry's description of Voldemort's recent activities, the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Magic" \o "Ministry of Magic" Ministry of Magic and many others in the magical world refuse to believe that Voldemort has returned. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-phoenix-plot-19" [19] In an attempt to counter and eventually discredit Dumbledore, who along with Harry is the most prominent voice in the wizarding world attempting to warn of Voldemort's return, the Ministry appoints  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolores_Umbridge" \o "Dolores Umbridge" Dolores Umbridge as the High Inquisitor of Hogwarts and the new Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher. She transforms the school into a dictatorial regime and refuses to allow the students to learn ways to defend themselves against dark magic. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-hp-phoenix-plot-19" [19]With Ron and Hermione's suggestion, Harry reluctantly forms " HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dumbledore%27s_Army" \o "Dumbledore's Army" Dumbledore's Army," a secret study group aimed to teach his classmates the higher-level skills of Defence Against the Dark Arts that he has learned from his previous encounters with Dark wizards. An important prophecy concerning Harry and Lord Voldemort is revealed, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Ivory_Tower_1-20" [20] and Harry discovers that he and Voldemort have a painful connection, allowing Harry to view some of Voldemort's actions telepathically. In the novel's climax, Harry and his friends face off against Voldemort's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_Eaters" \o "Death Eaters" Death Eaters at the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Magic" \o "Ministry of Magic" Ministry of Magic. Although the timely arrival of members of the Order of the Phoenix saves the children's lives,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sirius_Black" \o "Sirius Black" Sirius Black is killed in the conflict.In the sixth book,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" \o "Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince" Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince, Voldemort begins waging open warfare. Harry and his friends are relatively protected from that danger at Hogwarts. They are subject to all the difficulties of adolescence—Harry eventually begins dating Ginny, Ron establishes a strong infatuation with fellow Hogwarts student  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavender_Brown" \o "Lavender Brown" Lavender Brown, and Hermione starts recognizing her loving feelings for Ron. Near the beginning of the novel, Harry is given an old potions textbook filled with many annotations and recommendations signed by a mysterious writer, named "the Half-Blood Prince." This book is a source of scholastic success and great recognition from their new potions master,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horace_Slughorn" \o "Horace Slughorn" Horace Slughorn, but because of the potency of the spells that are written in it, becomes a source of concern. Harry takes private lessons with Dumbledore, who shows him various memories concerning the early life of Voldemort in a device called the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pensieve" \o "Pensieve" Pensieve. These reveal that Voldemort, to preserve his life, has split his soul into pieces, creating a series of HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horcrux" \o "Horcrux" horcruxes, evil enchanted items hidden in various locations, one of which was the diary destroyed in the second book. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-harry-potter-prince-21" [21] Harry's snobbish adversary, Draco Malfoy, attempts to attack Dumbledore, and the book culminates in the killing of Dumbledore by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professor_Snape" \o "Professor Snape" Professor Snape, the titular Half-Blood Prince. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" \o "Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows" Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows, the last book in the series, begins directly after the events of the sixth book. Lord Voldemort has completed his ascension to power and gains control of the Ministry of Magic. Harry, Ron and Hermione drop out of school so that they can find and destroy Voldemort's remaining horcruxes. To ensure their own safety as well as that of their family and friends, they are forced to isolate themselves. As they search for the horcruxes, the trio learns details about Dumbledore's past, as well as Snape's true motives—he had worked on Dumbledore's behalf since the murder of Harry's mother.The book culminates in the Battle of Hogwarts. Harry, Ron and Hermione, in conjunction with members of the Order of the Phoenix and many of the teachers and students, defend Hogwarts from Voldemort, his Death Eaters, and various dangerous  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magical_creatures_(Harry_Potter)" \o "Magical creatures (Harry Potter)" magical creatures. Several major characters are killed in the first wave of the battle, including  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remus_Lupin" \o "Remus Lupin" Remus Lupinand  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fred_Weasley" \o "Fred Weasley" Fred Weasley. After learning that he himself is a horcrux, Harry surrenders himself to Voldemort in the Forbidden Forest, who casts a killing curse at him. However, the defenders of Hogwarts do not surrender after learning this, but continue to fight on. Having managed to return from the dead, Harry finally faces Voldemort, whose horcruxes have all been destroyed. In the subsequent battle, Voldemort's killing curse rebounds off of Harry's spell and kills Voldemort, disintegrating his physical presence.An epilogue describes the lives of the surviving characters and the effects of Voldemort's death on the wizarding world.Supplementary worksSee also:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Rowling" \l "Philanthropy" \o "J. K. Rowling" J. K. Rowling: PhilanthropyRowling has expanded the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_universe" \o "Harry Potter universe" Harry Potter universe with several short books produced for various charities. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-22" [22] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-23" [23] In 2001, she released  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them" \o "Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them" Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them(a purported Hogwarts textbook) and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quidditch_Through_the_Ages" \o "Quidditch Through the Ages" Quidditch Through the Ages (a book Harry reads for fun). Proceeds from the sale of these two books benefitted the charity  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comic_Relief" \o "Comic Relief" Comic Relief. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-24" [24]In 2007, Rowling composed seven handwritten copies of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tales_of_Beedle_the_Bard" \o "The Tales of Beedle the Bard" The Tales of Beedle the Bard, a collection of fairy tales that is featured in the final novel, one of which was auctioned to raise money for the Children's High Level Group, a fund for mentally disabled children in poor countries. The book was published internationally on 4 December 2008. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-fetches-25" [25] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-26" [26]Rowling also wrote an 800-word  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_prequel" \o "Harry Potter prequel" prequel in 2008 as part of a fundraiser organised by the bookseller  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waterstones" \o "Waterstones" Waterstones. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-27" [27] All three of these books contain extra information about the Wizarding World not included in the original novels. In 2011, Rowling launched a new website announcing an upcoming project called  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pottermore" \o "Pottermore" Pottermore. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-28" [28] Pottermore opened to the general public on 14 April 2012. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-waiting-29" [29] Pottermore allows users to be sorted, be chosen by their wand and play various minigames. The main purpose of the website however was to allow the user to journey though the story with access to content not revealed by JK Rowling previously, with over 18,000 words of additional content. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-30" [30]Structure and genreSee also:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_influences_and_analogues" \o "Harry Potter influences and analogues" Harry Potter influences and analoguesThe Harry Potter novels fall within the genre of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasy_literature" \o "Fantasy literature" fantasy literature; however, in many respects they are also  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bildungsroman" \o "Bildungsroman" bildungsromans, or  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coming_of_age" \o "Coming of age" coming of age novels, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-31" [31] and contain elements of HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mystery_(fiction)" \o "Mystery (fiction)" mystery, adventure,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thriller_(genre)" \o "Thriller (genre)" thriller, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romance_novel" \o "Romance novel" romance. They can be considered part of the British children's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_story" \o "School story" boarding school genre, which includes  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" \o "Rudyard Kipling" Rudyard Kipling's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalky_%26_Co." \o "Stalky & Co." Stalky & Co.,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enid_Blyton" \o "Enid Blyton" Enid Blyton's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malory_Towers" \o "Malory Towers" Malory Towers,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Clare%27s_series" \o "St. Clare's series" St. Clare's and the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naughtiest_Girl" \o "Naughtiest Girl" Naughtiest Girl series, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Hamilton_(writer)" \o "Charles Hamilton (writer)" Frank Richards's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billy_Bunter" \o "Billy Bunter" Billy Bunter novels: the Harry Potter books are predominantly set in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hogwarts" \o "Hogwarts" Hogwarts, a fictional British boarding school for wizards, where the curriculum includes the use of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_(Harry_Potter)" \o "Magic (Harry Potter)" magic. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_Boarding-32" [32] In this sense they are "in a direct line of descent from  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Hughes" \o "Thomas Hughes" Thomas Hughes's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tom_Brown%27s_School_Days" \o "Tom Brown's School Days" Tom Brown's School Days and other Victorian and Edwardian novels of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_school_(UK)" \o "Public school (UK)" British public school life". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-33" [33] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-34" [34] They are also, in the words of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_King" \o "Stephen King" Stephen King, "shrewd mystery tales", HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Wild_About_Harry-35" [35] and each book is constructed in the manner of a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" \o "Sherlock Holmes" Sherlock Holmes-style  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mystery_fiction" \o "Mystery fiction" mystery adventure. The stories are told from a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_person_limited" \o "Third person limited" third person limited point of view with very few exceptions (such as the opening chapters of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" \o "Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone" Philosopher's Stone,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" \o "Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire" Goblet of Fire and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" \o "Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows" Deathly Hallows and the first two chapters of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half_Blood_Prince" \o "Harry Potter and the Half Blood Prince" Half-Blood Prince).In the middle of each book, Harry struggles with the problems he encounters, and dealing with them often involves the need to violate some school rules. If students are caught breaking rules, they are often disciplined by Hogwarts professors. However, the stories reach their climax in the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer_term" \o "Summer term" summer term, near or just after  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Final_examination" \o "Final examination" final exams, when events escalate far beyond in-school squabbles and struggles, and Harry must confront either  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voldemort" \o "Voldemort" Voldemort or one of his followers, the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_Eaters" \o "Death Eaters" Death Eaters, with the stakes a matter of life and death–a point underlined, as the series progresses, by one or more characters being killed in each of the final four books. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_Last_Adventure-36" [36] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-37" [37] In the aftermath, he learns important lessons through exposition and discussions with  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_teacher" \o "Head teacher" head teacher and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mentor" \o "Mentor" mentor  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" \o "Albus Dumbledore" Albus Dumbledore. In the final novel,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" \o "Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows" Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows, Harry and his friends spend most of their time away from Hogwarts, and only return there to face Voldemort at the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%A9nouement" \o "Dénouement" dénouement. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_Last_Adventure-36" [36]ThemesAccording to Rowling, a major theme in the series is death: "My books are largely about death. They open with the death of Harry's parents. There is Voldemort's obsession with conquering death and his quest for  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immortality" \o "Immortality" immortality at any price, the goal of anyone with magic. I so understand why Voldemort wants to conquer death. We're all frightened of it." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Geordie_Greig-6" [6]Academics and journalists have developed many other interpretations of themes in the books, some more complex than others, and some including  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Harry_Potter" \o "Politics of Harry Potter" political subtexts. Themes such as  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normality_(behavior)" \o "Normality (behavior)" normality, oppression, survival, and overcoming imposing odds have all been considered as prevalent throughout the series. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Greenwald2005-38" [38] Similarly, the theme of making one's way through adolescence and "going over one's most harrowing ordeals—and thus coming to terms with them" has also been considered. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Duffy2002-39" [39] Rowling has stated that the books comprise "a prolonged argument for tolerance, a prolonged plea for an end to  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bigotry" \o "Bigotry" bigotry" and that also pass on a message to "question authority and... not assume that the establishment or the press tells you all of the truth". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-40" [40]While the books could be said to comprise many other themes, such as power/abuse of power, love, prejudice, and free choice, they are, as Rowling states, "deeply entrenched in the whole plot"; the writer prefers to let themes "grow organically", rather than sitting down and consciously attempting to impart such ideas to her readers. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-QuickQuoteQuill-7" [7] Along the same lines is the ever-present theme of adolescence, in whose depiction Rowling has been purposeful in acknowledging her characters' sexualities and not leaving Harry, as she put it, "stuck in a state of permanent pre-pubescence". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Favourite_chapter-41" [41] Rowling said that, to her, the moral significance of the tales seems "blindingly obvious". The key for her was the choice between what is right and what is easy, "because that ... is how tyranny is started, with people being  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apathetic" \o "Apathetic" apathetic and taking the easy route and suddenly finding themselves in deep trouble." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-42" [42]Origins and publishing history HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:J._K._Rowling_2010.jpg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/J._K._Rowling_2010.jpg/180px-J._K._Rowling_2010.jpg" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:J._K._Rowling_2010.jpg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET The novelist,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._K._Rowling" \o "J. K. Rowling" J. K. Rowling.In 1990, Rowling was on a crowded train from  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester" \o "Manchester" Manchester to London when the idea for Harry suddenly "fell into her head". Rowling gives an account of the experience on her website saying: HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_falls_into_author.27s_head-43" [43]"I had been writing almost continuously since the age of six but I had never been so excited about an idea before. I simply sat and thought, for four (delayed train) hours, and all the details bubbled up in my brain, and this scrawny, black-haired, bespectacled boy who did not know he was a wizard became more and more real to me."Rowling completed Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone in 1995 and the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manuscript" \o "Manuscript" manuscript was sent off to several prospective  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_agent" \o "Literary agent" agents. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-44" [44] The second agent she tried, Christopher Little, offered to represent her and sent the manuscript to Bloomsbury. After eight other publishers had rejected Philosopher's Stone, Bloomsbury offered Rowling a £2,500 advance for its publication. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-45" [45] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Ivory_Tower_2-46" [46] Despite Rowling's statement that she did not have any particular  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_profile" \o "Demographic profile" age group in mind when beginning to write the Harry Potter books, the publishers initially targeted children aged nine to eleven. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-47" [47] On the eve of publishing, Rowling was asked by her publishers to adopt a more  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epicenity" \o "Epicenity" gender-neutral pen name in order to appeal to the male members of this age group, fearing that they would not be interested in reading a novel they knew to be written by a woman. She elected to use J. K. Rowling (Joanne Kathleen Rowling), using her grandmother's name as her second name because she has no  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_name" \o "Middle name" middle name. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Ivory_Tower_2-46" [46] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-48" [48] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_wordmark_(British).svg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Harry_Potter_wordmark_%28British%29.svg/250px-Harry_Potter_wordmark_%28British%29.svg.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_wordmark_(British).svg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET The logo used in British editionsHarry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone was published by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomsbury_Publishing" \o "Bloomsbury Publishing" Bloomsbury, the publisher of all Harry Potter books in the United Kingdom, on 30 June 1997. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-49" [49] It was released in the United States on 1 September 1998 by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholastic_Press" \o "Scholastic Press" Scholastic—the American publisher of the books—as Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-50" [50] after Rowling had received US$105,000 for the American rights—an unprecedented amount for a children's book by a then-unknown author. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-51" [51] Fearing that American readers would not associate the word "philosopher" with a magical theme (although the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosopher%27s_Stone" \o "Philosopher's Stone" Philosopher's Stone is alchemy-related), Scholastic insisted that the book be given the title Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone for the American market.The second book, Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets was originally published in the UK on 2 July 1998 and in the US on 2 June 1999. Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban was then published a year later in the UK on 8 July 1999 and in the US on 8 September 1999. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_UK_Release_Dates-52" [52] Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire was published on 8 July 2000 at the same time by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomsbury" \o "Bloomsbury" Bloomsbury and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholastic_Press" \o "Scholastic Press" Scholastic. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-53" [53] Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix is the longest book in the series at 766 pages in the UK version and 870 pages in the US version. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-54" [54] It was published worldwide in English on 21 June 2003. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-55" [55] Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince was published on 16 July 2005, and it sold 9 million copies in the first 24 hours of its worldwide release. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-56" [56] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-finale_sales-57" [57] The seventh and final novel, Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows, was published 21 July 2007. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-58" [58] The book sold 11 million copies in the first 24 hours of release, breaking down to 2.7 million copies in the UK and 8.3 million in the US. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-finale_sales-57" [57]TranslationsMain article:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_in_translation" \o "Harry Potter in translation" Harry Potter in translationThe series has been translated into 67 languages, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Translations_for_Harry_Potter-3" [3] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-59" [59] placing Rowling among the most translated authors in history. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-60" [60] The books have seen translations to diverse languages such as  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" \o "Azerbaijani language" Azerbaijani,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_language" \o "Ukrainian language" Ukrainian,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language" \o "Arabic language" Arabic,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu_language" \o "Urdu language" Urdu,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi_language" \o "Hindi language" Hindi,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengali_language" \o "Bengali language" Bengali,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welsh_language" \o "Welsh language" Welsh,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afrikaans" \o "Afrikaans" Afrikaans,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albanian_language" \o "Albanian language" Albanian,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvian_language" \o "Latvian language" Latvian and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnamese_language" \o "Vietnamese language" Vietnamese. The first volume has been translated into  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" \o "Latin" Latin and even  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek" \o "Ancient Greek" Ancient Greek, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-61" [61] making it the longest published work in Ancient Greek since the novels of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heliodorus_of_Emesa" \o "Heliodorus of Emesa" Heliodorus of Emesa in the 3rd century AD. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-62" [62]Some of the translators hired to work on the books were well-known authors before their work on Harry Potter, such as  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viktor_Golyshev" \o "Viktor Golyshev" Viktor Golyshev, who oversaw the Russian translation of the series' fifth book. The  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_language" \o "Turkish language" Turkish translation of books two to seven was undertaken by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sevin_Okyay" \o "Sevin Okyay" Sevin Okyay, a popular literary critic and cultural commentator. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-63" [63] For reasons of secrecy, translation can only start when the books are released in English; thus there is a lag of several months before the translations are available. This has led to more and more copies of the English editions being sold to impatient fans in non-English speaking countries. Such was the clamour to read the fifth book that its English language edition became the first English-language book ever to top the best-seller list in France. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-64" [64]The United States editions have been adapted into  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English" \o "American English" American English, to make them more understandable to a young American audience. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-65" [65]Completion of the seriesIn December 2005, Rowling stated on her web site, "2006 will be the year when I write the final book in the Harry Potter series." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-66" [66] Updates then followed in her  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Online_diary" \o "Online diary" online diarychronicling the progress of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" \o "Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows" Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows, with the release date of 21 July 2007. The book itself was finished on 11 January 2007 in the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balmoral_Hotel" \o "Balmoral Hotel" Balmoral Hotel, Edinburgh, where she scrawled a message on the back of a bust of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermes" \o "Hermes" Hermes. It read: "J. K. Rowling finished writing Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows in this room (552) on 11 January 2007." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-67" [67]Rowling herself has stated that the last chapter of the final book (in fact, the epilogue) was completed "in something like 1990". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-last_chapter-68" [68] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-last_chapter_means_epilogue-69" [69] In June 2006, Rowling, on an appearance on the British talk show  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_%26_Judy" \o "Richard & Judy" Richard & Judy, announced that the chapter had been modified as one character "got a reprieve" and two others who previously survived the story had in fact been killed. On 28 March 2007, the cover art for the Bloomsbury Adult and Child versions and the Scholastic version were released. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-70" [70] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-71" [71]In September 2012, Rowling mentioned in an interview that she might go back to make a "director's cut" of two of the existing Harry Potter books. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-72" [72]AchievementsCultural impactFor more details on this topic, see  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_fandom" \o "Harry Potter fandom" Harry Potter fandom. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_Platform_Kings_Cross.jpg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Harry_Potter_Platform_Kings_Cross.jpg/170px-Harry_Potter_Platform_Kings_Cross.jpg" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_Platform_Kings_Cross.jpg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET "Platform 9¾" sign on HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" \o "London King's Cross railway station" London King's Cross railway stationFans of the series were so eager for the latest instalment that bookstores around the world began holding events to coincide with the midnight release of the books, beginning with the 2000 publication of Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire. The events, commonly featuring mock sorting, games, face painting, and other live entertainment have achieved popularity with Potter fans and have been highly successful in attracting fans and selling books with nearly nine million of the 10.8 million initial print copies of Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince sold in the first 24 hours. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_casts_spell_at_checkouts-73" [73] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Potter_book_smashes_sales_records-74" [74] The final book in the series, Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows became the fastest selling book in history, moving 11 million units in the first twenty-four hours of release. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-75" [75] The series has also gathered adult fans, leading to the release of two editions of each Harry Potterbook, identical in text but with one edition's cover artwork aimed at children and the other aimed at adults. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-76" [76] Besides meeting online through blogs,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Podcast" \o "Podcast" podcasts, and fansites, Harry Potter super-fans can also meet at Harry Potter  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_conference" \o "Academic conference" symposia.The word Muggle has spread beyond its Harry Potter origins, becoming one of few pop culture words to land in the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" \o "Oxford English Dictionary" Oxford English Dictionary. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-77" [77]The Harry Potter fandom has embraced podcasts as a regular, often weekly, insight to the latest discussion in the fandom. Both  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MuggleCast" \o "MuggleCast" MuggleCast and HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PotterCast" \o "PotterCast" PotterCast HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-apple-enews-78" [78] have reached the top spot of iTunes podcast rankings and have been polled one of the top 50 favourite podcasts. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-pr-newswire-mc-79" [79]Commercial successSee also:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_best-selling_books" \o "List of best-selling books" List of best-selling books HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_lines.jpg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Harry_Potter_lines.jpg/250px-Harry_Potter_lines.jpg" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_lines.jpg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET Crowd outside a book store for the midnight release of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" \o "Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince" Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince.The popularity of the Harry Potter series has translated into substantial financial success for Rowling, her publishers, and other Harry Potter related license holders. This success has made Rowling the first and thus far only billionaire author. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-80" [80] The books have sold more than 400 million copies worldwide and have also given rise to the popular  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_adaptation" \o "Film adaptation" film adaptations produced by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros." \o "Warner Bros." Warner Bros.,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" \o "List of highest-grossing films" all of which have been highly successful in their own right. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-boxofficemojo-81" [81] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-82" [82] The films have in turn spawned eight video games and have led to the licensing of more than 400 additional Harry Potter products (including an  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod" \o "IPod" iPod). The Harry Potter brand has been estimated to be worth as much as $15 billion. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-HP_brand_worth-8" [8]The great demand for Harry Potter books motivated the New York Times to create a separate best-seller list for children's literature in 2000, just before the release of Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire. By 24 June 2000, Rowling's novels had been on the list for 79 straight weeks; the first three novels were each on the hardcover best-seller list. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-NYT_2000.2F06.2F24-83" [83] On 12 April 2007,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barnes_%26_Noble" \o "Barnes & Noble" Barnes & Noble declared thatDeathly Hallows had broken its  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-order" \o "Pre-order" pre-order record, with more than 500,000 copies pre-ordered through its site. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-84" [84] For the release ofGoblet of Fire, 9,000  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FedEx" \o "FedEx" FedEx trucks were used with no other purpose than to deliver the book. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-ew-gof-midnight-85" [85] Together, Amazon.com and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barnes_%26_Noble" \o "Barnes & Noble" Barnes & Noble pre-sold more than 700,000 copies of the book. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-ew-gof-midnight-85" [85] In the United States, the book's initial printing run was 3.8 million copies. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-ew-gof-midnight-85" [85] This record statistic was broken by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" \o "Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix" Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix, with 8.5 million, which was then shattered by Half-Blood Prince with 10.8 million copies. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-cnn-hbp-86" [86] 6.9 million copies of Prince were sold in the U.S. within the first 24 hours of its release; in the United Kingdom more than two million copies were sold on the first day. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-bbc-hbp-record-87" [87] The initial U.S. print run for Deathly Hallows was 12 million copies, and more than a million were pre-ordered through Amazon and Barnes & Noble. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-88" [88]Awards, honours, and recognitionThe Harry Potter series have been the recipients of a host of awards since the initial publication of Philosopher's Stone including four Whitaker Platinum Book Awards (all of which were awarded in 2001), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-89" [89] three  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9_Smarties_Book_Prize" \o "Nestlé Smarties Book Prize" Nestlé Smarties Book Prizes (1997–1999), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-90" [90] two  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scottish_Arts_Council" \o "Scottish Arts Council" Scottish Arts Council Book Awards (1999 and 2001), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-91" [91] the inaugural  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Costa_Book_Awards" \o "Costa Book Awards" Whitbread children's book of the year award (1999), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-92" [92] the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Book_Awards" \o "British Book Awards" WHSmith book of the year (2006), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-93" [93] among others. In 2000,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" \o "Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban" Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban was nominated for a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugo_Award_for_Best_Novel" \o "Hugo Award for Best Novel" Hugo Award for Best Novel, and in 2001,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" \o "Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire" Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire won said award. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-94" [94] Honours include a commendation for the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnegie_Medal_(literary_award)" \o "Carnegie Medal (literary award)" Carnegie Medal (1997), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-95" [95] a short listing for the HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guardian_Award" \o "Guardian Award" Guardian Children's Award (1998), and numerous listings on the notable books, editors' Choices, and best books lists of the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Library_Association" \o "American Library Association" American Library Association, The New York Times, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Public_Library" \o "Chicago Public Library" Chicago Public Library, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publishers_Weekly" \o "Publishers Weekly" Publishers Weekly. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-96" [96]A 2004 study found that books in the series were commonly read aloud in elementary schools in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_County,_California" \o "San Diego County, California" San Diego County, California. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-97" [97] Based on a 2007 online poll, the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Education_Association" \o "National Education Association" National Education Association in the U.S. listed the series in its "Teachers' Top 100 Books for Children." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-NEA2007-98" [98] Three of the books (Sorcerer’s Stone, Prisoner of Azkaban, and Goblet of Fire) were among the "Top 100 Chapter Books" of all time in a 2012 poll by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_Library_Journal" \o "School Library Journal" School Library Journal. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-SLJChapter2012-99" [99]ReceptionLiterary criticism HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_british_books.jpg"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Harry_Potter_british_books.jpg/250px-Harry_Potter_british_books.jpg" \* MERGEFORMATINET  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_british_books.jpg" \o "Enlarge"  INCLUDEPICTURE "http://bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.24wmf1/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" \* MERGEFORMATINET British editions of the seven Harry Potterbooks. L-R: books  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince" \o "Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince" 6,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" \o "Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows" 7,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" \o "Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone" 1,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" \o "Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets" 2,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" \o "Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban" 3,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" \o "Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire" 4, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix" \o "Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix" 5.Early in its history, Harry Potter received positive reviews. On publication, the first volume, Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone, attracted attention from the Scottish newspapers, such as  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Scotsman" \o "The Scotsman" The Scotsman, which said it had "all the makings of a classic", HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-newspaper-reviews-hp-ps-100" [100] and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Herald_(Glasgow)" \o "The Herald (Glasgow)" The Glasgow Herald, which called it "Magic stuff". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-newspaper-reviews-hp-ps-100" [100] Soon the English newspapers joined in, with more than one comparing it to  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roald_Dahl" \o "Roald Dahl" Roald Dahl's work:  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Mail_on_Sunday" \o "The Mail on Sunday" The Mail on Sunday rated it as "the most imaginative debut since Roald Dahl", HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-newspaper-reviews-hp-ps-100" [100] a view echoed by  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" \o "The Sunday Times" The Sunday Times("comparisons to Dahl are, this time, justified"), HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-newspaper-reviews-hp-ps-100" [100] while  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian" \o "The Guardian" The Guardian called it "a richly textured novel given lift-off by an inventive wit". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-newspaper-reviews-hp-ps-100" [100]By the time of the release of the fifth volume, Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix, the books began to receive strong criticism from a number of literary scholars. Yale professor, literary scholar, and critic  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Bloom" \o "Harold Bloom" Harold Bloom raised criticisms of the books' literary merits, saying, "Rowling's mind is so governed by clichés and dead metaphors that she has no other style of writing." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-101" [101]  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A._S._Byatt" \o "A. S. Byatt" A. S. Byattauthored a New York Times op-ed article calling Rowling's universe a "secondary secondary world, made up of intelligently patchworked derivative motifs from all sorts of children's literature ... written for people whose imaginative lives are confined to TV cartoons, and the exaggerated (more exciting, not threatening) mirror-worlds of soaps, reality TV and celebrity gossip". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Harry_Potter_and_the_Childish_Adult-102" [102] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Rosen" \o "Michael Rosen" Michael Rosen, a novelist and poet, advocated the books were not suited for children, who would be unable to grasp the complex themes. Rosen also stated that "J. K. Rowling is more of an adult writer." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-103" [103] The critic  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Holden" \o "Anthony Holden" Anthony Holden wrote in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Observer" \o "The Observer" The Observer on his experience of judging  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban" \o "Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban" Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban for the  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Whitbread_Awards" \o "1999 Whitbread Awards" 1999 Whitbread Awards. His overall view of the series was negative—"the Potter saga was essentially patronising, conservative, highly derivative, dispiritingly nostalgic for a bygone Britain", and he speaks of "pedestrian, ungrammatical prose style". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-104" [104]  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ursula_K._Le_Guin" \o "Ursula K. Le Guin" Ursula K. Le Guin said, "I have no great opinion of it. When so many adult critics were carrying on about the 'incredible originality' of the first Harry Potter book, I read it to find out what the fuss was about, and remained somewhat puzzled; it seemed a lively kid's fantasy crossed with a "school novel", good fare for its age group, but stylistically ordinary, imaginatively derivative, and ethically rather mean-spirited." HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-105" [105]By contrast, author  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fay_Weldon" \o "Fay Weldon" Fay Weldon, while admitting that the series is "not what the poets hoped for", nevertheless goes on to say, "but this is not poetry, it is readable, saleable, everyday, useful prose". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Rowling_books_.27for_people_with_stunted_imaginations.27-106" [106] The literary critic A. N. Wilson praised the Harry Potter series in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times" \o "The Times" The Times, stating: "There are not many writers who have JK's Dickensian ability to make us turn the pages, to weep—openly, with tears splashing—and a few pages later to laugh, at invariably good jokes ... We have lived through a decade in which we have followed the publication of the liveliest, funniest, scariest and most moving children's stories ever written". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-107" [107] Charles Taylor of  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salon.com" \o "Salon.com" Salon.com, who is primarily a movie critic, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-108" [108] took issue with Byatt's criticisms in particular. While he conceded that she may have "a valid cultural point—a teeny one—about the impulses that drive us to reassuring pop trash and away from the troubling complexities of art", HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-A.S._Byatt_and_the_goblet_of_bile-109" [109] he rejected her claims that the series is lacking in serious  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_merit" \o "Literary merit" literary merit and that it owes its success merely to the childhood reassurances it offers. Taylor stressed the progressively darker tone of the books, shown by the murder of a classmate and close friend and the psychological wounds and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_isolation" \o "Social isolation" social isolation each causes. Taylor also argued that Philosopher's Stone, said to be the most light-hearted of the seven published books, disrupts the childhood reassurances that Byatt claims spur the series' success: the book opens with news of a  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_murder" \o "Double murder" double murder, for example. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-A.S._Byatt_and_the_goblet_of_bile-109" [109] HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_King" \o "Stephen King" Stephen King called the series "a feat of which only a superior imagination is capable", and declared "Rowling's punning, one-eyebrow-cocked sense of humor" to be "remarkable". However, he wrote that despite the story being "a good one", he is "a little tired of discovering Harry at home with his horrible aunt and uncle", the formulaic beginning of all seven books. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Wild_About_Harry-35" [35] King has also joked that "Rowling's never met an adverb she did not like!" He does however predict that Harry Potter "will indeed stand time's test and wind up on a shelf where only the best are kept; I think Harry will take his place with  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_(Alice%27s_Adventures_in_Wonderland)" \o "Alice (Alice's Adventures in Wonderland)" Alice,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huckleberry_Finn" \o "Huckleberry Finn" Huck,  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" \o "Frodo Baggins" Frodo, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dorothy_Gale" \o "Dorothy Gale" Dorothy and this is one series not just for the decade, but for the ages". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-110" [110]Social impactsAlthough  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine)" \o "Time (magazine)" Time magazine named Rowling as a runner-up for its 2007  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_Person_of_the_Year" \o "Time Person of the Year" Person of the Year award, noting the social, moral, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Harry_Potter" \o "Politics of Harry Potter" political inspiration she has given  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter_fandom" \o "Harry Potter fandom" her fandom, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-111" [111]cultural comments on the series have been mixed.  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Post" \o "Washington Post" Washington Post book critic Ron Charles opined in July 2007 that the large numbers of adults reading the Potter series but few other books may represent a "bad case of cultural infantilism", and that the straightforward "good vs. evil" theme of the series is "childish". He also argued "through no fault of Rowling's", the cultural and marketing "hysteria" marked by the publication of the later books "trains children and adults to expect the roar of the coliseum, a mass-media experience that no other novel can possibly provide". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-112" [112]Librarian Nancy Knapp pointed out the books' potential to improve  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy" \o "Literacy" literacy by motivating children to read much more than they otherwise would. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Knapp2003InDefenseOfHP-113" [113] Agreeing about the motivating effects, Diane Penrod also praised the books' blending of simple entertainment with "the qualities of highbrow literary fiction", but expressed concern about the distracting effect of the prolific  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merchandising" \o "Merchandising" merchandising that accompanies the book launches. HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-114" [114]Jennifer Conn used Snape's and Quidditch coach Madam Hooch's teaching methods as examples of what to avoid and what to emulate in clinical teaching, HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-115" [115] and Joyce Fields wrote that the books illustrate four of the five main topics in a typical first-year sociology class: "sociological concepts including culture, society, and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialisation" \o "Socialisation" socialisation;  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stratification" \o "Social stratification" stratification and HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_inequality" \o "Social inequality" social inequality;  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_institutions" \o "Social institutions" social institutions; and  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_theory" \o "Social theory" social theory". HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Potter" \l "cite_note-Fields2007HPSociologicalImagination-116" [116]Jenny Sawyer wrote in  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Science_Monitor" \o "Christian Science Monitor" Christian Science Monitor on 25 July 2007 that the books represent a "disturbing trend in commercial storytelling and Western society" in that stories "moral center [sic] have all but vanished from much of today's  HYPERLINK "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_culture" \o "Popular culture" pop culture ... after 10 years, 4,195 pages, and over 375 million copies, J. K. Rowling's towering achievement lacks the cornerstone of almost all great children's literature: the hero's moral journey".
